  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0a0e8a6a-471a-4a73-bf54-a771ce31f645'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer16072706573404190985">In this thrilling sequel to AMULET #1: THE STONEKEEPER, Emily and her brother Navin head for Kanalis, a beautiful and mysterious city of waterfalls, where they hope to find the antidote for the poison that felled their mother. That cure lies in the eggs of a giant serpent atop Demon's Head Mountain, but the kids' archenemy, Trellis, is headed for the peak, too. A battle th</span>
  <span id="freeText16072706573404190985" style="display:none">In this thrilling sequel to AMULET #1: THE STONEKEEPER, Emily and her brother Navin head for Kanalis, a beautiful and mysterious city of waterfalls, where they hope to find the antidote for the poison that felled their mother. That cure lies in the eggs of a giant serpent atop Demon's Head Mountain, but the kids' archenemy, Trellis, is headed for the peak, too. A battle that will engulf all of Kanalis is looming. It's up to Em to triumph over evil while controlling the amulet's power . . . without losing herself!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16072706573404190985" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_24800350').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_24800350').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_24800350').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

  <span id="freeText15467062611598636904" style="display:none">My niece is <i>really</i> into this graphic novel series and <i>really</i> wanted me and wife to read the books...so we're reading the books. <br /><br />This is a kitchen sink adventure with evil elves, a sort-of medieval time period <i>and</i> steampunk elements, a samurai styled warrior, anthropomorphic characters, a mystical forest, and a "chosen one" girl who needs to realize her hidden power and harness it to save the world. This mishmash of tropes and a story we've seen before would normally mean a dull book, but this worked for me. Also, this was meant for kids (probably around 8 to 10) and I'm willing to cut it a good deal of slack.<br /><br />The pictures are pretty good. There are a few that make you linger over the scene, taking it in and all the gorgeous details.<br /><br />All in all this is real good stuff and I would have loved it when I was a kid!</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2948291108" />
    <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt"><img alt="Rebecca McNutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602390057p2/36977686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2948291108?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca McNutt" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt">Rebecca McNutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2948291108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13945106853149140817">In elementary school (way back in 2008 when the Amulet series was brand new), I'd had a lot of trouble getting into the first book in the series, mainly because its tragic scenes felt very overblown and unrealistic, but also because there seemed to be a lot of lacking character development for some of the book's most intriguing ones. I decided to go back and give this series another chance, continuing on with the 2nd one. I definitely found <i>The Stonekeeper's Curse</i> a lot better than the 1st book,</span>
  <span id="freeText13945106853149140817" style="display:none">In elementary school (way back in 2008 when the Amulet series was brand new), I'd had a lot of trouble getting into the first book in the series, mainly because its tragic scenes felt very overblown and unrealistic, but also because there seemed to be a lot of lacking character development for some of the book's most intriguing ones. I decided to go back and give this series another chance, continuing on with the 2nd one. I definitely found <i>The Stonekeeper's Curse</i> a lot better than the 1st book, especially since Trellis the elf boy is given much more of a background (a rather tragic background which explains his antagonistic behaviour while at the same time showing that he's not really evil, he's just trying to stay on his father's good side). Emily also gets a lot more depth in this book than in the 1st, and her family story isn't as preachy.<br /><br />The world-building in <i>The Stonekeeper's Curse</i> is incredible and the graphic illustrations bring it to life very well. A few new characters are also introduced, and the book includes many well-done suspenseful moments, as well as emotional and endearing moments which give it more depth than the typical dark fantasy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13945106853149140817" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4875018667919691478">Not as fun as the first one, but definitely expanded the world and the threat. I really liked the bad guy, and the obvious Zuko knockoff is still great, despite being an obvious Zuko knockoff. This series really hits the middle grade spot.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2271092605" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2271092605" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2271092605?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brian Yahn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brian Yahn" href="/user/show/22849115-brian-yahn">Brian Yahn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2271092605" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17524197237255271497">The second installment of Amulet is basically Pacific Rim meets Narnia.<br/><br/>Like Pacific Rim, this issue walked dangerously close to becoming mindless action. But it was able to distinguish itself with all the clever and fun intricacies of the world.<br/><br/>On the one hand, the uniqueness from the first issue started to wear off. The protagonist's arch got a little too close to The Lord of the Rings. But on the other hand, for the first half of the issue, while Kazu Kibuishi was building up the world of Amul</span>
  <span id="freeText17524197237255271497" style="display:none">The second installment of Amulet is basically Pacific Rim meets Narnia.<br /><br />Like Pacific Rim, this issue walked dangerously close to becoming mindless action. But it was able to distinguish itself with all the clever and fun intricacies of the world.<br /><br />On the one hand, the uniqueness from the first issue started to wear off. The protagonist's arch got a little too close to The Lord of the Rings. But on the other hand, for the first half of the issue, while Kazu Kibuishi was building up the world of Amulet, it was just too creative and wonderful to mater.<br /><br />I'm slightly worried the world building and character introductions seemed to stop at the midpoint. But I'm hoping that in the next issues, the magic in this world has some deeper meaning, that really ties into the characters.<br /><br />I'll definitely be reading more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17524197237255271497" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

You can find it below ! )<br /><br /><b>Disclaimer</b>: i may complain a bit in this review, lol, in the vein of: <b>Raise your hand if you think the Goodreads mobile app needs a COMPLETE overhaul! <i>*RAISES HAND EMPHATICALLY* </i></b><br />It is so ridiculous how horrible the app is and there really is no excuse for it! <br />I’m very sorry about the following frustrating story, and my many a complaint about the GR app, and <i>you don’t have to read the stuff in <u>BOLD brackets</u> if you don’t want to</i>, and yes I am aware of the irony that is the fact that I COULD’VE just written my review a third time instead of going on a tangent out of frustration... but it happened. Its done. And i just COULD NOT bring myself to do it, Lol. <br /><br />All right guys; listen – I feel bad, but there is no way, <i>LIT-ER-AL-LY</i>,<br />No possible way in existence that I can write this review over AGAIN, at this point in time.<br />It would be the THIRD time in a row. And i am just like... nope. <br />(Post-posting Afterthought- I DID write a micro-review below! Please give it a read!)<br />*refrains from screaming out of frustration*<br /><br /> <b>[</b> 😩😩😩 The app crashed when I was about to post my FIRST (impromptu- hence not being SAVED 😢) full review, then it <br />crashed a SECOND time during my attempt at staying positive:<br /><b>Review Number 2</b>- the “not so great as the first one but I have strep throat, and I TRIED, so not a bad sum up?” review. <br />Well, Goodreads crashed A-GAIN <br /><i>(surprise, surprise// this app seriously needs a major overhaul, amIright, folks?)</i> After Attempt Number TWO being so mercilessly effing DESTROYEDDDDD as well... I hope you understand and thanks for stickin’ with me 😅)</i> <b>]</b><br /><br /><br /><i><u>But! I did write <b>this</b></u>:</i><br /><br /><b>MINI REVIEW</b> v <b>MINI REVIEW</b> v <b>MINI REVIEW</b>!<br /><i>***This book was TRULY so incredible, an absolute gem for all fantasy lovers, especially fans of the “portal writing” trope, &amp; anime/manga &amp; Miyazaki lovers! But really, its for everyone. It is an incredibly imaginative, beautifully told tale, with UNREAL artwork. Like... just so INCREDIBLY GORGEOUS you could look at it over and over and still be stricken by the sheer fantastical beauty of it all. The pages that are dedicated to one panel, to one piece of art, truly are like looking at a still from a Miyazaki film (but even more beautiful if that is possible?) Its INCREDIBLE! In every way. World building, character development... storyline, art.... its got it all, guys</i>. <br /><br />GIVE. THIS. A. SHOT! If you love fantasy, especially portal trope lovers! Even if you have only dipped your toes into graphic novels.... read this!***<br /><br /><b>Really, please don’t get turned around by my mixed moods- be aware- This book was a WIN! In all ways. </b><br /><i>My complaints have 0 to do with the book. This book was... everything you could want in a fantasy story and more.</i><br /><br /><b>[</b> Can I just say,<br /><br /><b>O M F G the GR app <i>NEEDS</i> TO BE UPDATED</b>! <br />WHY OH WHY DO I <i>EVER</i> EVEN USE IT INSTEAD OF JUST GOING TO THE BROWSER VERSION OF GR ON SAFARI ? <br />😭😭😭<br /><br />WHY? <br /><br />TORTURE? I’m pretty sure <b>I</b> don’t care that much. I’m just being dramatic bc i’m sick &amp; frustrated. Please excuse my outburst. 😉😂😂). <b>]</b></span>

    <a title="Maxwell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell"><img alt="Maxwell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539318702p2/1381728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1158829682?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maxwell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maxwell" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell">Maxwell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1381728-maxwell?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1158829682" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1855169837360749600"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I'll admit, I wasn't a huge fan of the first volume. But I wanted to give the series another try, so I checked this out from the library. And I was much more impressed with this volume.<br/><br/>The art, same as the first volume, is <i>beautiful</i>. Kibuishi has an amazing style that is whimsical and fantastic. He also creates great characters. Cogsley and Miskit are two super cool sidekicks. And the walking house! I want one.<br/><br/>The story definitely picks up in this volume. You get more conflict, some bac</span>
  <span id="freeText1855169837360749600" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />I'll admit, I wasn't a huge fan of the first volume. But I wanted to give the series another try, so I checked this out from the library. And I was much more impressed with this volume.<br /><br />The art, same as the first volume, is <i>beautiful</i>. Kibuishi has an amazing style that is whimsical and fantastic. He also creates great characters. Cogsley and Miskit are two super cool sidekicks. And the walking house! I want one.<br /><br />The story definitely picks up in this volume. You get more conflict, some back story, and some good character development from Emily and Navin. I really liked their parallel storylines in this one. <br /><br />My only minor qualm with this series is that because it's for children, a lot of things resolve nice and tidy, so I'm never really concerned for the characters. However, it doesn't shy away from some violence and intense action scenes.<br /><br />I'm glad I continued on with this series, and that I checked out Volume 3 from the library as well!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1855169837360749600" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1354847297" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8036563689760494416">The elves are getting close and the action ramps up as Emily and Navin race to find a cure for the poison that is killing their mom. Emily must learn to control the stone as it fights to try and take control of her. This was even better than the first volume! </span>

The villain is BIG in this story. Emily is being forced to learn to control her new found power. I can't wait to read more.</span>

<div id="review_2172906529" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2172906529" />
    <a title="Kati " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6553210-kati"><img alt="Kati " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551827809p2/6553210.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2172906529?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kati " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kati " href="/user/show/6553210-kati">Kati </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6553210-kati?shelf=favorites-books">favorites-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2172906529" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1220482899646643090">Yes! I just love and adore this graphic novel series so much! This amazing series is most definitely on my top favorite graphic novel list. I don't want to go into any details about the second volume of the Amulet series, but it starts off where the first volume left off at. Emily is now the new stone keeper master of a very powerful stone. She and her beloved brother Navin are trying to save there mother from a poison. I won't say what kind of poison it is or how their mother got poison, becaus</span>
  <span id="freeText1220482899646643090" style="display:none">Yes! I just love and adore this graphic novel series so much! This amazing series is most definitely on my top favorite graphic novel list. I don't want to go into any details about the second volume of the Amulet series, but it starts off where the first volume left off at. Emily is now the new stone keeper master of a very powerful stone. She and her beloved brother Navin are trying to save there mother from a poison. I won't say what kind of poison it is or how their mother got poison, because that is spoiler you just have to read this amazing graphic novel to find out what I am talking about. Believe me it is so worth to read this graphic novel I think you all will love this fantastic graphic novel! I fell in love with it from the very first few chapters in while I read it in the first volume. But in the second volume Emily and Navin along with their misfit crew the head too a beautiful and mystery city, where there are amazing and very gorgeous waterfalls surrounding the big city. The graphic art of the city is so gorgeous and very detail I just couldn't stop staring at the art all day long. The beautiful city is called Kanalis they all went to the city in hopes to find an antidote for Emily and Navin mother who is dying if she doesn't get the antidote in time. But when they first land in Kanalis they all met new people and friends who have been waiting for both Emily and Navin for years. While there in Kanalis there enemy's is right behind them and new dangers &amp; adventures ensues after they are in the big city of Kanalis. Everything changes for both Emily and Navin right there and than . Both Emily and Navin find out some truth and secrets about the world they are in and they also find out about legends truths about themselves and there family and about their future in the strange world they all are in. Now I won't say what their future is about or if it gets better or worst for them because spoiler. But when I first found out about there legend future including the secrets and truth about the world from the start. I wanted to read and learn more and more about the secrets and legends. But of course I have to read the rest of the next volumes of the Amulet series to found out more. I am going to stop here without getting too spoiler. But I do highly recommend the Amulet series it is absolutely an amazingly and fantastic graphic novel that I truly love and enjoy thoroughly. The graphic art is my favorite part while reading this novels because the art is really gorgeous and very detailed I just can't get enough seeing the art. All and all you can clearly see I totally love and adore the Amulet series that I can't wait to read the next volumes of this series soon! </span>
  <a data-text-id="1220482899646643090" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5735773184538930026">Not as good as the first one, it was pretty much the same story line with Emily yet again trying to save her mum and her struggling with her amulet powers. <br/><br/>I didn't like that apart from Emily and her mum there were no other female characters, Emily was always surrounded by guys. <br/><br/>The artwork was on point though, it was the most enjoyable aspect. I especially loved the pages where there was just one large panel of some kind of scenery, they were beautifully drawn.<br/></span>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer74417024" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3386894582949256915">Book two in the Amulet series from Kibuishi. This series hasn't quite grabbed me completely yet. For the most part I really like the artwork (although sometimes there's a certain flatness to the character designs that's a little annoying), and the story seems to be going places -- it's just moving REALLY SLOWLY. I think this will appeal to young fans of Jeff Smith's Bone, but unlike Bone it's not likely to have much cross-generational appeal.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lCXKSx5B+MKZKmEb12k7LGgGCKTscfTny+eVAhACErpfyzFxrS2v9H9ZZKJ5nnNDtLDt2R0Y0GYT7lNQQOXODA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15179856615914592561">Kazu Kibuishi (born 1978) is an American graphic novel author and illustrator. He is best known for being the creator and editor of the comic anthology <i>Flight</i> and for creating the webcomic <i>Copper</i>. He has also written (drawn) the <i>Amulet series</i>. The webcomic artist and noted critic Scott McCloud has said that some of Kazu Kibuishi's work is so beautifully drawn that "it hurts my hands when I look at</span>
  <span id="freeText15179856615914592561" style="display:none">Kazu Kibuishi (born 1978) is an American graphic novel author and illustrator. He is best known for being the creator and editor of the comic anthology <i>Flight</i> and for creating the webcomic <i>Copper</i>. He has also written (drawn) the <i>Amulet series</i>. The webcomic artist and noted critic Scott McCloud has said that some of Kazu Kibuishi's work is so beautifully drawn that "it hurts my hands when I look at it".</span>
